<p><b>Palm Beach County</b> is a <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">county</a> located in the <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, directly north of <a href="/wiki/Broward_County,_Florida" title="Broward County, Florida">Broward County</a>. As of the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 census</a>, the population was 1,320,134,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QF_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-QF-1">[1]</a></sup> making it the third-most populous county in Florida. The largest city and <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">county seat</a> is <a href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="West Palm Beach, Florida">West Palm Beach</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR6_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-GR6-2">[2]</a></sup> Named after one of its oldest settlements, <a href="/wiki/Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="Palm Beach, Florida">Palm Beach</a>, the county was established in 1909, after being split from <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County,_Florida" title="Miami-Dade County, Florida">Dade County</a>. The county's modern-day boundaries were established in 1963. Palm Beach County is one of the three counties in <a href="/wiki/South_Florida" title="South Florida">South Florida</a> which make up the <a href="/wiki/Miami_metropolitan_area" title="Miami metropolitan area">Miami metropolitan area</a>, which was home to an estimated 6,012,331 people at the 2015 census.</p>
<p>The area had been increasing in population since the late 19th century, with the incorporation of West Palm Beach in 1894 and after <a href="/wiki/Henry_Flagler" title="Henry Flagler">Henry Flagler</a> extended the <a href="/wiki/Florida_East_Coast_Railway" title="Florida East Coast Railway">Florida East Coast Railway</a> and built the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Poinciana_Hotel" title="Royal Poinciana Hotel">Royal Poinciana Hotel</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Breakers_(hotel)" title="The Breakers (hotel)">The Breakers</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flagler_Museum" title="Flagler Museum">Whitehall</a>. In 1928, the <a href="/wiki/1928_Okeechobee_hurricane" title="1928 Okeechobee hurricane">Okeechobee hurricane</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" title="Landfall (meteorology)">struck</a> West Palm Beach and caused thousands of deaths. More recently, the county acquired national attention during the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2000" title="United States presidential election, 2000">2000 presidential election</a>, when a <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Florida,_2000#Recount" title="United States presidential election in Florida, 2000">controversial recount occurred</a>.</p>
<p>As of 2004, Palm Beach County is Florida's wealthiest county, with a <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_personal_income_in_the_United_States" title="Per capita personal income in the United States">per capita personal income</a> of $44,518.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> It leads the state in agricultural productivity, agriculture is Palm Beach County's 2nd largest industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Approximately 10,200 years ago, Native Americans began migrating into Florida. The tribes settling in modern-day Palm Beach County included the <a href="/wiki/Ais_people" title="Ais people">Ais</a>', <a href="/wiki/Calusa" title="Calusa">Calusas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaega" title="Jaega">Jaegas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mayaimi" title="Mayaimi">Mayaimis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tequesta" title="Tequesta">Tequestas</a>. An estimated 20,000 Native Americans lived in South Florida when the Spanish arrived. Their population diminished significantly by the 18th century, due to warfare, enslavement, and diseases from Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> In 1513, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de León">Juan Ponce de León</a>, who led a European expedition to Florida earlier that year, became the first non-Native American to reach Palm Beach County, after landing in the modern day Jupiter area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Among the first non-Native American residents were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">African Americans</a>, many of whom were former slaves or immediate descendants of former slaves who had escaped to Florida from slave plantations located in <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a>. Runaway African slaves started coming to what was then <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Spanish Florida</a> in the late 17th century and they found refuge among the <a href="/wiki/Seminole" title="Seminole">Seminole</a> Native Americans. During the <a href="/wiki/Seminole_Wars" title="Seminole Wars">Seminole Wars</a>, these African-American slaves fought with the Seminoles against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">White</a> settlers and bounty hunters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blacksites_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-blacksites-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Portions of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Seminole_War" title="Second Seminole War">Second Seminole War</a> occurred in Palm Beach County, including the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jupiter_Inlet" title="Battle of Jupiter Inlet">Battle of Jupiter Inlet</a> in 1838.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Royal_Poinciana,_Palm_Beach,_Florida,_1900.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5369" data-file-width="7148" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/The_Royal_Poinciana%2C_Palm_Beach%2C_Florida%2C_1900.jpg/220px-The_Royal_Poinciana%2C_Palm_Beach%2C_Florida%2C_1900.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/The_Royal_Poinciana%2C_Palm_Beach%2C_Florida%2C_1900.jpg/330px-The_Royal_Poinciana%2C_Palm_Beach%2C_Florida%2C_1900.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/The_Royal_Poinciana%2C_Palm_Beach%2C_Florida%2C_1900.jpg/440px-The_Royal_Poinciana%2C_Palm_Beach%2C_Florida%2C_1900.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Royal_Poinciana,_Palm_Beach,_Florida,_1900.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Royal Poinciana Hotel in 1900</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The oldest surviving structure, the <a href="/wiki/Jupiter_Inlet_Light" title="Jupiter Inlet Light">Jupiter Lighthouse</a>, was built in 1860, after receiving authorization to the land from President <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Pierce" title="Franklin Pierce">Franklin Pierce</a> in 1854.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jlh_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-jlh-10">[10]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, Florida was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederate States of America</a>. To aid the cause of their state, Augustus O. Lang and James Paine removed the lighting mechanism, dimming the lighthouse and assisting their <a href="/wiki/Blockade_runner" title="Blockade runner">blockade runners</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pbchojil_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-pbchojil-11">[11]</a></sup> Lang was also the first white settler in Palm Beach County. He built a palmetto shack along the eastern shore of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Worth_Lagoon" title="Lake Worth Lagoon">Lake Worth</a> in 1863 after abandoning the cause of the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederacy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> After the Civil War ended, the Jupiter Lighthouse was re-lit in 1866.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pbchojil_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-pbchojil-11">[11]</a></sup> Thirteen years later, a <a href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service" title="National Weather Service">National Weather Service</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service_Miami,_Florida" title="National Weather Service Miami, Florida">office</a> was established at the lighthouse complex. However, the office was moved to <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a> after that city's population began to rapidly grow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwsmiamihistory_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-nwsmiamihistory-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 1873, a <a href="/wiki/1873_Atlantic_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Five" title="1873 Atlantic hurricane season">hurricane</a> caused a shipwreck between <a href="/wiki/Biscayne_Bay" title="Biscayne Bay">Biscayne Bay</a> and the <a href="/wiki/New_River_(Broward_County,_Florida)" title="New River (Broward County, Florida)">New River</a>. The crew survived, but nearly died due to starvation because of the desolation of the area. An Act of Congress on June 20, 1874, resulted in the establishment of five houses of <a href="/wiki/Houses_of_Refuge_in_Florida" title="Houses of Refuge in Florida">Houses of Refuge</a> along the east coast of Florida from the <a href="/wiki/Fort_Pierce_Inlet_State_Park" title="Fort Pierce Inlet State Park">Fort Pierce Inlet</a> southward to Biscayne Bay. Orange Grove House of Refuge No. 3 was built near <a href="/wiki/Delray_Beach,_Florida" title="Delray Beach, Florida">Delray Beach</a> in 1876.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Henry_Flagler" title="Henry Flagler">Henry Flagler</a>, who was instrumental in the county's development in the late 19th century and early 20th century, first visited in 1892, describing the area as a "veritable paradise." Flagler subsequently purchased land on both sides of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Worth_Lagoon" title="Lake Worth Lagoon">Lake Worth</a>. Other investors followed suit, causing a small boom and bringing in existing businesses or new ones were established. The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Poinciana_Hotel" title="Royal Poinciana Hotel">Royal Poinciana Hotel</a>, constructed by Flagler to accommodate wealthy tourists, opened for business in February 1894. About a month later, the <a href="/wiki/Florida_East_Coast_Railway" title="Florida East Coast Railway">Florida East Coast Railway</a>, owned by Flagler, reached West Palm Beach. On November 5, 1894, Palm Beach County's oldest city, West Palm Beach, was incorporated. In 1896, another hotel built by Flagler was opened, the Palm Beach Inn, later renamed <a href="/wiki/The_Breakers_(hotel)" title="The Breakers (hotel)">The Breakers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> He also constructed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flagler_Museum" title="Flagler Museum">his own winter home</a> beginning in 1900; he and his wife moved in on February 6, 1902. Flagler died there on May 20, 1913, after falling down a flight of marble stairs.</p>
<p>Palm Beach County was created in 1909. It was named for its first settled community, <a href="/wiki/Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="Palm Beach, Florida">Palm Beach</a>. The County was carved out of what was then the northern portion of <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County,_Florida" title="Miami-Dade County, Florida">Dade County</a>, comprising part of the areas now occupied by <a href="/wiki/Okeechobee_County,_Florida" title="Okeechobee County, Florida">Okeechobee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Broward_County,_Florida" title="Broward County, Florida">Broward</a> counties, part of <a href="/wiki/Martin_County,_Florida" title="Martin County, Florida">Martin</a> and all of Palm Beach county, initially including all of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Okeechobee" title="Lake Okeechobee">Lake Okeechobee</a>. The southernmost part of Palm Beach County was separated to create the northern portion of Broward County in 1915, the northwestern portion became part of Okeechobee County 1917 and southern Martin County was created from northernmost Palm Beach County in 1925.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-courthouse_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-courthouse-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1928_Okeechobee_Aftermath_17.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="457" data-file-width="690" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/1928_Okeechobee_Aftermath_17.jpg/220px-1928_Okeechobee_Aftermath_17.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/1928_Okeechobee_Aftermath_17.jpg/330px-1928_Okeechobee_Aftermath_17.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/1928_Okeechobee_Aftermath_17.jpg/440px-1928_Okeechobee_Aftermath_17.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1928_Okeechobee_Aftermath_17.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A montage of images of impact by the Okeechobee hurricane</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Early on September 17, 1928, the <a href="/wiki/1928_Okeechobee_hurricane" title="1928 Okeechobee hurricane">Okeechobee hurricane</a> made landfall near West Palm Beach and crossed Lake Okeechobee shortly thereafter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-17">[17]</a></sup> Storm surge left severe damage in the city of Palm Beach, and a death toll of 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mwr-westindian_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-mwr-westindian-18">[18]</a></sup> In West Palm Beach, more than 1,711 homes were destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Further inland, wind-driven storm surge in Lake Okeechobee inundated adjacent communities, particularly <a href="/wiki/Belle_Glade,_Florida" title="Belle Glade, Florida">Belle Glade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pahokee,_Florida" title="Pahokee, Florida">Pahokee</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Bay,_Florida" title="South Bay, Florida">South Bay</a>. Hundreds of square miles were flooded, including some areas with up to 20 feet (6.1 m) of water. Numerous houses were swept away and damaged after crashing into other obstacles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sptimes_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-sptimes-20">[20]</a></sup> Flood waters did not completely subside for several weeks. At least 2,500 deaths occurred, many of whom were black migrant farmers. Damage in South Florida totaled approximately $25 million (1928 <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">USD</a>). In response to the storm, the <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Hoover_Dike" title="Herbert Hoover Dike">Herbert Hoover Dike</a> was constructed to prevent a similar disaster.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwsokeechobee_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-nwsokeechobee-21">[21]</a></sup> Previously, Lake Okeechobee overflowed in 1926 during the <a href="/wiki/1926_Miami_hurricane" title="1926 Miami hurricane">Miami hurricane</a>, though flooding was primarily in <a href="/wiki/Moore_Haven,_Florida" title="Moore Haven, Florida">Moore Haven</a> in <a href="/wiki/Glades_County,_Florida" title="Glades County, Florida">Glades County</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nwsmiami_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-nwsmiami-22">[22]</a></sup> As a result of both the Okeechobee and Miami hurricanes, Palm Beach County, along with the rest of South Florida, began suffering economic turmoil and pushed the region into the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, even before the <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Crash_of_1929" title="Wall Street Crash of 1929">Wall Street Crash of 1929</a>. Housing prices dropped dramatically in the county, as well as in the rest of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Palm_Beach_International_Airport" title="Palm Beach International Airport">Palm Beach International Airport</a> (PBIA), then known as Morrison's Field, opened in 1936. After the United States entered <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, it was converted to an <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_Air_Force_Base&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Palm Beach Air Force Base (page does not exist)">Air Force Base</a> in 1942.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBIA_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-PBIA-24">[24]</a></sup> During the war, thousands of servicemen arrived in Palm Beach County for training and supporting the war effort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_War_II_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-World_War_II-25">[25]</a></sup> Following the conclusion of World War II, a number of veterans returned to the area for work, vacation, or retirement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_War_II_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-World_War_II-25">[25]</a></sup> The base was closed and became a commercial airport again in 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBIA_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-PBIA-24">[24]</a></sup> Migration to the county by workers, tourists, and retirees continued into the 21st century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>August 28, 1949, a Category 4 <a href="/wiki/1949_Florida_hurricane" title="1949 Florida hurricane">hurricane</a> struck West Palm Beach with <a href="/wiki/Maximum_sustained_wind" title="Maximum sustained wind">maximum sustained winds</a> of 150 mph (240 km/h) causing considerable damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BestTrack_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-BestTrack-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>The area's first television station, <a href="/wiki/WIRK" title="WIRK">WIRK</a>-TV Channel 21, signed on September 13, 1953. It went off the air less than three years later. However, <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/WPTV-TV" title="WPTV-TV">WPTV-TV</a> and <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/WPEC" title="WPEC">WPEC</a> first aired in 1954 and 1955, respectively – both of which are still in existence today.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Richard_Paul_Pavlick" title="Richard Paul Pavlick">Richard Paul Pavlick</a> nearly attempted to assassinate then President-elect <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> in <a href="/wiki/Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="Palm Beach, Florida">Palm Beach</a> in December 1960. <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_family" title="Kennedy family">The Kennedys</a> were vacationing at La Guerida,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-postman_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-postman-29">[29]</a></sup> a house originally owned by <a href="/wiki/Rodman_Wanamaker" title="Rodman Wanamaker">Rodman Wanamaker</a> and sold to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joseph_P._Kennedy,_Sr." title="Joseph P. Kennedy, Sr.">Joseph P. Kennedy, Sr.</a> in 1933.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Pavlick's anti-Catholic and anti-government views led him to stalk and plot to kill JFK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hate_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-hate-31">[31]</a></sup> A resident of <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>, Pavlick loaded-up his car with sticks of dynamite and drove down to Palm Beach. Pavlick sent bizarre postcards to his hometown, which included information that coincided with the Kennedys vacation. The postmaster alerted the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secret_Service" title="United States Secret Service">Secret Service</a> to be vigilant for Pavlick's vehicle. On December 11, as Kennedy was preparing to leave for <a href="/wiki/Mass_(liturgy)" title="Mass (liturgy)">Mass</a>, Pavlick forwent his attempt to murder Kennedy because he was with his wife, <a href="/wiki/Jacqueline_Kennedy_Onassis" title="Jacqueline Kennedy Onassis">Jacqueline</a>, and their two children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-postman_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-postman-29">[29]</a></sup> On December 15, Pavlick's car, which had sticks of dynamite inside, was surrounded by police and he was arrested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-postman_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-postman-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hate_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-hate-31">[31]</a></sup> Charges against Pavolick were dropped on December 2, 1963, 10 days after <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_F._Kennedy" title="Assassination of John F. Kennedy">Kennedy was assassinated</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dallas,_Texas" title="Dallas, Texas">Dallas, Texas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-postman_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-postman-29">[29]</a></sup> Additionally, a secret <a href="/wiki/Detachment_Hotel" title="Detachment Hotel">blast shelter</a> built on <a href="/wiki/Peanut_Island" title="Peanut Island">Peanut Island</a> during his presidency because escalating <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> tensions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>About three-quarters of Lake Okeechobee was removed from Palm Beach County in 1963 and divided up among <a href="/wiki/Glades_County,_Florida" title="Glades County, Florida">Glades</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hendry_County,_Florida" title="Hendry County, Florida">Hendry</a>, Martin and Okeechobee counties. This was the final change to the county's boundaries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-courthouse_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-courthouse-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_David" title="Hurricane David">Hurricane David</a> struck near West Palm Beach late on September 3, 1979, with sustained winds of 100 mph (155 km/h). The storm's winds shattered windows in stores near the coast and caused property damage, including blowing the frame off the Palm Beach Jai Alai and downing the 186-foot (57-m) <a href="/wiki/WJNO" title="WJNO">WJNO</a> AM radio tower in West Palm Beach into the Intracoastal Waterway. A few roofs were torn off, and numerous buildings were flooded from over 6 inches (150 mm) of rainfall. Damage in the county reached $30 million (1979 USD), most of which was incurred to agriculture.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Butterfly_Ballot,_Florida_2000_(large).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="917" data-file-width="1437" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Butterfly_Ballot%2C_Florida_2000_%28large%29.jpg/220px-Butterfly_Ballot%2C_Florida_2000_%28large%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Butterfly_Ballot%2C_Florida_2000_%28large%29.jpg/330px-Butterfly_Ballot%2C_Florida_2000_%28large%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Butterfly_Ballot%2C_Florida_2000_%28large%29.jpg/440px-Butterfly_Ballot%2C_Florida_2000_%28large%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Butterfly_Ballot,_Florida_2000_(large).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The "butterfly ballot" used during the 2000 election in Palm Beach County</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The county became the center of controversy during <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2000" title="United States presidential election, 2000">presidential election</a> on November 7, 2000. Allegedly, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Florida,_2000" title="United States presidential election in Florida, 2000">"butterfly ballot"</a>, designed by Palm Beach County Supervisor of Elections <a href="/wiki/Theresa_LePore" title="Theresa LePore">Theresa LePore</a>, led to an unexpectedly large number of votes for <a href="/wiki/Reform_Party_of_the_United_States_of_America" title="Reform Party of the United States of America">Reform Party</a> candidate <a href="/wiki/Pat_Buchanan" title="Pat Buchanan">Pat Buchanan</a>, rather than for <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrat</a> <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>. Due to the aforementioned "butterfly ballot" and the closeness of the statewide results between Gore and <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Texas" title="Governor of Texas">Texas Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a>, manual recounts were conducted. On December 8, The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Florida_Supreme_Court" title="Florida Supreme Court">Florida Supreme Court</a> voted 4-3 to mandate manual recounts in all counties with disputed results. However, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a> overturned the decision in <a href="/wiki/Bush_v._Gore" title="Bush v. Gore">Bush v. Gore</a> on December 12, allowing <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_of_Florida" title="Secretary of State of Florida">Florida Secretary of the State</a> <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Harris" title="Katherine Harris">Katherine Harris</a> to award the 25 electoral votes to Bush, as Harris's tally prior to the state-ordered recounts placed him ahead of Gore by 537 popular votes. In turn, this gave Bush victory in the national election.</p>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> in 2001, an <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">FBI</a> investigation revealed that 12 of the 19 terrorists trained or resided in Palm Beach County during the months prior to the attacks, including <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_al-Ghamdi" title="Ahmed al-Ghamdi">Ahmed al-Ghamdi</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nationalspot_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-nationalspot-33">[33]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_al-Haznawi" title="Ahmed al-Haznawi">Ahmed al-Haznawi</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-34">[34]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marwan_al-Shehhi" title="Marwan al-Shehhi">Marwan al-Shehhi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waleed_Alshehri" title="Waleed Alshehri">Waleed</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wail_Alshehri" title="Wail Alshehri">Wail Alshehri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Satam_al-Suqami" title="Satam al-Suqami">Satam al-Suqami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Atta" title="Mohamed Atta">Mohamed Atta</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nationalspot_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-nationalspot-33">[33]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ziad_Jarrah" title="Ziad Jarrah">Ziad Jarrah</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-34">[34]</a></sup> Later that month, during the <a href="/wiki/2001_anthrax_attacks" title="2001 anthrax attacks">anthrax attacks</a>, a letter containing <a href="/wiki/Anthrax" title="Anthrax">spores</a> of this substance was mailed to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Media_(publisher)" title="American Media (publisher)">American Media, Inc.</a> building in Boca Raton. Three people were exposed to the anthrax, including <a href="/wiki/Robert_Stevens_(photo_editor)" title="Robert Stevens (photo editor)">Robert Stevens</a>, a photo editor who died after an infection induced by the anthrax.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nationalspot_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-nationalspot-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Frances_05_sept_2004_1815Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6800" data-file-width="5200" height="288" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Hurricane_Frances_05_sept_2004_1815Z.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Frances_05_sept_2004_1815Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Hurricane_Frances_05_sept_2004_1815Z.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Frances_05_sept_2004_1815Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Hurricane_Frances_05_sept_2004_1815Z.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Frances_05_sept_2004_1815Z.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Frances_05_sept_2004_1815Z.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Satellite imagery of Hurricane Frances making landfall in Martin County</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Palm Beach County was impacted by several tropical cyclones in 2004 and 2005, most severely by hurricanes <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Frances" title="Hurricane Frances">Frances</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jeanne" title="Hurricane Jeanne">Jeanne</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Wilma</a>, which resulted in at least a few billion dollars in damage. Early on September 5, 2004, Frances made landfall in Martin County as a Category 2 hurricane with winds of 105 mph (165 km/h). Although the county recorded tropical storm-force winds, a wind gust of 91 mph (146 km/h) was observed at the Jupiter Inlet. The strong winds caused about 659,000 power outages, according to <a href="/wiki/Florida_Power_%26_Light" title="Florida Power &amp; Light">Florida Power &amp; Light</a> (FPL). Structural damage in Palm Beach County included 15,000 houses and 2,400 businesses. Additionally, crops suffered severely, with $70 million (2004 USD) in damage dealt to sugar cane. Six deaths occurred in Palm Beach County due to storm-related vehicle accidents or drownings.</p>
<p>About three weeks after Frances, Hurricane Jeanne struck near the same location as a Category 3 hurricane with winds of 120 mph (195 km/h). Despite Jeanne being more intense than Frances, the overall impact was slightly lesser. Storm surge of 2 to 4 ft (0.61 to 1.22 m) along the coast resulted in moderate beach erosion in Palm Beach County. Jeanne also brought strong winds, with a wind gust of 94 mph (151 km/h) recorded at the <a href="/wiki/Coastal-Marine_Automated_Network" title="Coastal-Marine Automated Network">C-MAN</a> station at the Lake Worth pier. Unofficially, a wind gust of 125 mph (201 km/h) was observed in West Palm Beach. FPL reported 591,300 electrical outages in the county after Jeanne. About 4,160 homes were damaged and 60 were destroyed. Severe local flooding occurred in <a href="/wiki/Jupiter,_Florida" title="Jupiter, Florida">Jupiter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palm_Beach_Gardens,_Florida" title="Palm Beach Gardens, Florida">Palm Beach Gardens</a>, and rural areas of western Palm Beach County. Agricultural losses reached about $30 million. Overall, Jeanne wrought $260 million in damage, but caused no deaths.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wilma05FLLandfallRadar.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="455" data-file-width="598" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Wilma05FLLandfallRadar.png/220px-Wilma05FLLandfallRadar.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Wilma05FLLandfallRadar.png/330px-Wilma05FLLandfallRadar.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Wilma05FLLandfallRadar.png/440px-Wilma05FLLandfallRadar.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wilma05FLLandfallRadar.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Radar imagery of Hurricane Wilma making landfall in Florida</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On October 24, 2005, Hurricane Wilma made landfall near <a href="/wiki/Cape_Romano" title="Cape Romano">Cape Romano</a>, Florida, as a Category 3 hurricane with winds of 120 mph (195 km/h). The storm headed northwestward and moved directly across Palm Beach County. At PBIA, sustained winds reached 82 mph (132 km/h), while a wind gust as strong as 101 mph (163 km/h) was observed. Winds damaged 52,385  Palm Beach County homes and destroyed 2,669 others.<a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.pbcgov.com/DES/affordable-housing/pdf/Chapter5.pdf" rel="nofollow">[1]</a></p>
<p>Since Hurricane Wilma in 2005, several other tropical cyclones have impacted Palm Beach County. In August 2008, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Fay_(2008)" title="Tropical Storm Fay (2008)">Tropical Storm Fay</a> brought generally minor flooding, with 7 to 9 in (180 to 230 mm) of rain over the eastern portions of the county. Fay spawned an EF2 over <a href="/wiki/Wellington,_Florida" title="Wellington, Florida">Wellington</a>, which deroofed stables and knocked over electrical poles and several trees at the Palm Beach Equine Clinic. Additionally, the Equine Veterinary lost more than 95% of its roof tiles and a heavy trailer was tossed about 120 ft (37 m) from its original location. An apartment building also suffered minor roof damage. About four years later, in August 2012, the outerbands of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Isaac_(2012)" title="Hurricane Isaac (2012)">Hurricane Isaac</a> dropped at least 15.86 in (403 mm) of rain near <a href="/wiki/Lion_Country_Safari" title="Lion Country Safari">Lion Country Safari</a>. The consequent flooding left neighborhoods, in <a href="/wiki/The_Acreage,_Florida" title="The Acreage, Florida">The Acreage</a>, Loxahatchee, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="Royal Palm Beach, Florida">Royal Palm Beach</a> and Wellington, stranded for up to several days. One man died after crashing into a concrete wall along <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95" title="Interstate 95">Interstate 95</a> during the storm. Overall, damage in the county totaled approximately $71.59 million (2012 USD).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_name_Palm_Beach">The name Palm Beach</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: The name Palm Beach">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coconut_palm" title="Coconut palm">coconut palm</a>, <i>Cocos nucifera</i>, is not native to Florida (nor anywhere else in the United States). Its presence in what is today Palm Beach County is due to the shipwreck of the Spanish ship Providencia in 1878, near today's <a href="/wiki/Mar-a-Lago" title="Mar-a-Lago">Mar-a-Lago</a>. It was traveling from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Havana,_Cuba" title="Havana, Cuba">Havana</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz,_Spain" title="Cádiz, Spain">Cádiz, Spain</a> with a cargo of coconuts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The shipwreck was within walking distance of the shore — the Florida State Archives conserves a picture<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> — and a deliberate grounding so as to obtain an insurance payout has been proposed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The coconuts were salvaged, too many to be eaten, and thousands were planted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> A lush grove of palm trees soon grew on what was later named Palm Beach.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Okeechobee.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Lake_Okeechobee.JPG/200px-Lake_Okeechobee.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Lake_Okeechobee.JPG/300px-Lake_Okeechobee.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Lake_Okeechobee.JPG/400px-Lake_Okeechobee.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lake_Okeechobee.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of Lake Okeechobee from <a href="/wiki/Pahokee,_Florida" title="Pahokee, Florida">Pahokee</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Census_Bureau" title="U.S. Census Bureau">U.S. Census Bureau</a>, the county has a total area of 2,383 square miles (6,170 km<sup>2</sup>), of which 1,970 square miles (5,100 km<sup>2</sup>) is land and 413 square miles (1,070 km<sup>2</sup>) (17.3%) is water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR1_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-GR1-42">[42]</a></sup> It is the second-largest county in Florida by land area and third-largest by total area. Much of the water is the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Okeechobee" title="Lake Okeechobee">Lake Okeechobee</a>. The county has approximately 526,000 acres (213,000 ha) of farmland.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjacent_counties">Adjacent counties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Adjacent counties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Palm Beach County borders <a href="/wiki/Martin_County,_Florida" title="Martin County, Florida">Martin County</a> to the north, the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to the east, <a href="/wiki/Broward_County,_Florida" title="Broward County, Florida">Broward County</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Hendry_County,_Florida" title="Hendry County, Florida">Hendry County</a> to the west, and extends into <a href="/wiki/Lake_Okeechobee" title="Lake Okeechobee">Lake Okeechobee</a> in the northwest, where it borders <a href="/wiki/Okeechobee_County,_Florida" title="Okeechobee County, Florida">Okeechobee County</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glades_County,_Florida" title="Glades County, Florida">Glades County</a> at one point in the center of the lake.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_areas">Natural areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Natural areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arthur_R._Marshall_Loxahatchee_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Arthur R. Marshall Loxahatchee National Wildlife Refuge">Arthur R. Marshall Loxahatchee National Wildlife Refuge</a>, a 147,392 acres (59,647 ha) refuge in <a href="/wiki/Boynton_Beach,_Florida" title="Boynton Beach, Florida">Boynton Beach</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/DuPuis_Management_Area" title="DuPuis Management Area">DuPuis Management Area</a>, a 21,875 acres (8,852 ha) area of protected lands.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/J.W._Corbett_Wildlife_Management_Area" title="J.W. Corbett Wildlife Management Area">J.W. Corbett Wildlife Management Area</a>, a 60,348 acres (24,422 ha) area of protected lands.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jupiter_Ridge_Natural_Area" title="Jupiter Ridge Natural Area">Jupiter Ridge Natural Area</a>, a 271 acres (110 ha) preserve in <a href="/wiki/Jupiter,_Florida" title="Jupiter, Florida">Jupiter, Florida</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Juno_Dunes_Natural_Area" title="Juno Dunes Natural Area">Juno Dunes Natural Area</a>, a 576 acres (233 ha) preserve in <a href="/wiki/Juno_Beach" title="Juno Beach">Juno Beach</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frenchman%27s_Forest_Natural_Area" title="Frenchman's Forest Natural Area">Frenchman's Forest Natural Area</a>, a 158 acres (64 ha) preserve in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palm_Beach_Gardens" title="Palm Beach Gardens">Palm Beach Gardens</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sweetbay_Natural_Area" title="Sweetbay Natural Area">Sweetbay Natural Area</a>, a 1,094 acres (443 ha) preserve in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palm_Beach_Gardens" title="Palm Beach Gardens">Palm Beach Gardens</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Royal_Palm_Beach_Pines_Natural_Area" title="Royal Palm Beach Pines Natural Area">Royal Palm Beach Pines Natural Area</a>, a 773 acres (313 ha) preserve in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Palm_Beach" title="Royal Palm Beach">Royal Palm Beach</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hypoluxo_Scrub_Natural_Area" title="Hypoluxo Scrub Natural Area">Hypoluxo Scrub Natural Area</a>, a 97 acres (39 ha) preserve in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hypoluxo" title="Hypoluxo">Hypoluxo</a>.</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rosemary_Scrub_Natural_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rosemary Scrub Natural Area (page does not exist)">Rosemary Scrub Natural Area</a>, a 14 acres (5.7 ha) preserve in Boynton Beach.</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Seacrest_Scrub_Natural_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Seacrest Scrub Natural Area (page does not exist)">Seacrest Scrub Natural Area</a>, a 54 acres (22 ha) preserve in Boynton Beach.</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Delray_Oaks_Natural_Area&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Delray Oaks Natural Area (page does not exist)">Delray Oaks Natural Area</a> a 25 acres (10 ha) prairie and xeric hammock preserve with a small strand swamp and areas of flatwoods in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delray_Beach" title="Delray Beach">Delray Beach</a>.</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Leon_M._Weekes_Environmental_Preserve&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Leon M. Weekes Environmental Preserve (page does not exist)">Leon M. Weekes Environmental Preserve</a>, a 12 acres (4.9 ha) preserve in Delray Beach.</li>
</ul>
<p>In addition the county has many coral reef patches along its coastline. The county has put in a lot of effort to preserve the reefs.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_Census">2010 Census</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2010 Census">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><u>U.S. Census Bureau 2010 Ethnic/Race Demographics:</u><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBdemo_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-PBdemo-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBD_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-PBD-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_People" title="White People">White</a> (73.5% when including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Hispanic" title="White Hispanic">White Hispanics</a>) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" title="White (U.S. Census)">White (non-Hispanic)</a>: 60.1% (10.8% German, 10.2% Irish, 9.4% Italian, 7.4% English, 4.7% Polish, 4.7% Russian, 2.4% French, 1.6% Scottish, 1.1% Scotch-Irish, 1.0% Dutch, 1.0% Hungarian, 0.8% Swedish, 0.7% Greek, 0.6% Norwegian, 0.6% French Canadian)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBdemo_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-PBdemo-48">[48]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">Hispanic</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">Latino</a> of any race: 19.0% (3.7% Mexican, 3.3% Cuban, 3.0% Puerto Rican, 1.7% Colombian, 1.5% Guatemalan, 0.8% Dominican, 0.6% Honduran, 0.6% Peruvian, 0.5% Salvadoran)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBD_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-PBD-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_(U.S._Census)" title="Black (U.S. Census)">Black (non-Hispanic)</a> (17.3% when including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_Hispanic" title="Black Hispanic">Black Hispanics</a>): 16.8% (7.2% <a href="/wiki/West_Indian" title="West Indian">West Indian</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Caribbean_American" title="Afro-Caribbean American">Afro-Caribbean American</a> [4.6% Haitian, 1.8% Jamaican, 0.2% Bahamian, 0.2% <a href="/wiki/Afro-Caribbean" title="Afro-Caribbean">Other or Unspecified West Indian</a>, 0.2% Trinidadian and Tobagonian, 0.1% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_West_Indian" title="British West Indian">British West Indian</a>,] 0.8% <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Subsaharan African</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBdemo_48-2"><a href="#cite_note-PBdemo-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBCAncestry_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-PBCAncestry-51">[51]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">Asian</a>: 2.4% (0.7% Asian Indian, 0.4% Chinese, 0.4% Other Asian, 0.3% Filipino, 0.3% Vietnamese, 0.1% Korean, 0.1% Japanese)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBdemo_48-3"><a href="#cite_note-PBdemo-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBD_49-2"><a href="#cite_note-PBD-49">[49]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">Two or more races</a>: 2.3%</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">American Indian and Alaska Native</a>: 0.5%</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_(U.S._Census)" title="Pacific Islander (U.S. Census)">Native Hawaiian and Other Pacific Islander</a>: 0.1%<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBdemo_48-4"><a href="#cite_note-PBdemo-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBD_49-3"><a href="#cite_note-PBD-49">[49]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">Other Races</a>: 4.0% (0.5% Arab)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBdemo_48-5"><a href="#cite_note-PBdemo-48">[48]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>In 2010, 4.5% of the population considered themselves to be of only "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_people" title="American people">American</a>" ancestry (regardless of race or ethnicity.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBdemo_48-6"><a href="#cite_note-PBdemo-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2010, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haitian_people" title="Haitian people">Haitians</a> made up the largest population of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigrant" title="Immigrant">immigrants</a>, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuban_people" title="Cuban people">Cuban</a> <a href="/wiki/Exile" title="Exile">exiled</a> <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugees</a> coming in second, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_people" title="Mexican people">Mexicans</a> in third, followed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colombian_people" title="Colombian people">Colombians</a> in fourth place, then <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamaican_people" title="Jamaican people">Jamaicans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guatemalan_people" title="Guatemalan people">Guatemalans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canadians" title="Canadians">Canadians</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honduran_people" title="Honduran people">Hondurans</a>, ninth being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peruvian_people" title="Peruvian people">Peruvians</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_people" title="Brazilian people">Brazilians</a> being the tenth highest group of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Expatriates" title="Expatriates">expatriates</a>. <a href="/wiki/British_people" title="British people">British</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_people" title="German people">Germans</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_people" title="Polish people">Polish</a>, which had held spots in Palm Beach County's top 10 immigrant list of 2000, dropped off the 2010 list, which now no longer has any <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_countries" title="European countries">European countries</a> in its top ten.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>There were 664,594 households out of which 24.35% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 46.28% were <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">married couples</a> living together, 11.68% had a female householder with no husband present, and 37.40% were non-families. 30.11% of all households were made up of individuals and 14.70% (4.02% male and 10.68% female) had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.39 and the average family size was 2.97.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBD_49-4"><a href="#cite_note-PBD-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBage_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-PBage-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>The age distribution is 20.4% under the age of 18, 8.0% from 18 to 24, 23.7% from 25 to 44, 26.4% from 45 to 64, and 21.6% who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 43.5 years. For every 100 females there were 93.8 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 91.3 males.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBage_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-PBage-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, 22.3% of the county's population was <a href="/wiki/Foreign_born" title="Foreign born">foreign born</a>, with 43.7% being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naturalized_citizen_of_the_United_States" title="Naturalized citizen of the United States">naturalized American citizens</a>. Of foreign-born residents, 71.3% were born in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, 13.6% were born in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, 9.2% born in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, 4.0% in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, 1.8% born in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, and 0.1% were born in <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBdemo_48-7"><a href="#cite_note-PBdemo-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of 2010, 73.13% of all residents spoke <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_language" title="Primary language">primary language</a>, while 15.69% spoke <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, 4.03% <a href="/wiki/French-based_creole_languages" title="French-based creole languages">French Creole</a> (mainly <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Creole" title="Haitian Creole">Haitian Creole</a>,) 1.06% <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, 0.94% <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, and 0.54% of the population spoke <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>. In total, 26.87% spoke languages other than English as their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mother_language" title="Mother language">mother language</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Companies headquartered in Palm Beach County include <a href="/wiki/Office_Depot" title="Office Depot">Office Depot</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_ADT_Corporation" title="The ADT Corporation">The ADT Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/TBC_Corporation" title="TBC Corporation">TBC Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/G4S_Secure_Solutions" title="G4S Secure Solutions">G4S Secure Solutions</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=BIOMET_3i&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="BIOMET 3i (page does not exist)">BIOMET 3i</a>, <a href="/wiki/Campus_Management_Corp." title="Campus Management Corp.">Campus Management Corp.</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cross_Match_Technologies&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cross Match Technologies (page does not exist)">Cross Match Technologies</a>, <a href="/wiki/NextEra_Energy" title="NextEra Energy">NextEra Energy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_GEO_Group" title="The GEO Group">The GEO Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bluegreen_Corporation" title="Bluegreen Corporation">Bluegreen Vacations</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Florida_Crystals&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Florida Crystals (page does not exist)">Florida Crystals</a>.</p>
<p>Although not headquartered in Palm Beach County there is a significant number of aerospace focused facilities operating in the northern part of the county. Aerospace companies with facilities located within the county include <a href="/wiki/United_Technologies" title="United Technologies">United Technologies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pratt_%26_Whitney_Rocketdyne" title="Pratt &amp; Whitney Rocketdyne">Pratt &amp; Whitney Rocketdyne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sikorsky_Aircraft" title="Sikorsky Aircraft">Sikorsky Aircraft</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_Dynamics" title="General Dynamics">General Dynamics</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Belcan_Engineering_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Belcan Engineering Group (page does not exist)">Belcan Engineering Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">Lockheed Martin</a>. Many of these companies rank among the top 100 employers for the county. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>A number of <a href="/wiki/Shopping_mall" title="Shopping mall">shopping malls</a> exist throughout Palm Beach County, including the <a href="/wiki/Boynton_Beach_Mall" title="Boynton Beach Mall">Boynton Beach Mall</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Gardens_Mall" title="The Gardens Mall">The Gardens Mall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Town_Center_at_Boca_Raton" title="Town Center at Boca Raton">Town Center at Boca Raton</a>, <a href="/wiki/CityPlace_(West_Palm_Beach)" title="CityPlace (West Palm Beach)">CityPlace</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Mall_at_Wellington_Green" title="The Mall at Wellington Green">The Mall at Wellington Green</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mizner_Park" title="Mizner Park">Mizner Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Formerly, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palm_Beach_Mall" title="Palm Beach Mall">Palm Beach</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cross_County_Plaza" title="Cross County Plaza">Cross County Malls</a> operated in the county, though they closed in 1997 and 2010, respectively.</p>
<p>In undeveloped (central and western) Palm Beach County there is significant agricultural production, especially <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plant_nurseries" title="Plant nurseries">nurseries</a>, truck crops (vegetables), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Palm Beach County has been called the "Winter Vegetable Capital" of the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>Previously <a href="/wiki/W._R._Grace_and_Company" title="W. R. Grace and Company">W. R. Grace and Company</a> had its headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_area" title="Unincorporated area">unincorporated</a> Palm Beach County, near <a href="/wiki/Boca_Raton,_Florida" title="Boca Raton, Florida">Boca Raton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BRClosing_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-BRClosing-59">[59]</a></sup> Prior to its closing, the Boca Raton headquarters had about 130 employees. On January 27, 2011 it announced it was closing the Boca headquarters and moving its administrative staff out of state along with some employees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BRClosing_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-BRClosing-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>Previously, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Media_(publisher)" title="American Media (publisher)">American Media</a>, publisher of the <a href="/wiki/National_Enquirer" title="National Enquirer">National Enquirer</a>, was headquartered in the Boca Raton. It still maintains an office there, but moved the National Enquirer to New York in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_income">Personal income</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Personal income">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>For 2010 the median income for a household in the county was $53,242, and the median income for a family was $64,445. Males had a median income of $44,324 versus $37,337 for females. The <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> for the county was $33,610. About 8.6% of families and 12.2% of the population were below the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poverty_line" title="Poverty line">poverty line</a>, including 18.5% of those under age 18 and 7.7% of those aged 65 or over.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Florida_Department_of_Corrections" title="Florida Department of Corrections">Florida Department of Corrections</a> operates the <a href="/wiki/Glades_Correctional_Institution" title="Glades Correctional Institution">Glades Correctional Institution</a> in an <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_area" title="Unincorporated area">unincorporated area</a> in Palm Beach County near <a href="/wiki/Belle_Glade,_Florida" title="Belle Glade, Florida">Belle Glade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="County_Government">County Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: County Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The county is governed by a <a href="/wiki/County_commission" title="County commission">Board of Commissioners</a>. The Board consists of seven commissioners, who are all elected from single-member districts. One of the commissioners is elected Mayor and one of them is elected Vice-Mayor.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Commissioners serve staggered terms, and Commissioners from Districts 1, 3, 5, and 7 are elected during presidential election years, while the Commissioners from Districts 2, 4, and 6 are elected in gubernatorial election years.</p>
<p>Elected county officers include a Clerk of Courts and Comptroller, <a href="/wiki/Sheriff" title="Sheriff">Sheriff</a>, Property Appraiser, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tax_Collector" title="Tax Collector">Tax Collector</a>, and Supervisor of Elections. State officers serving the Florida judicial district include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Attorney" title="State Attorney">State Attorney</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Defender" title="Public Defender">Public Defender</a>. All positions are four year terms, requiring direct election by voters in presidential election years.</p>
<p>Five former county commissioners have been accused or found guilty of corruption from 2006 to 2009. A grand jury recommended a strong <a href="/wiki/Inspector_general" title="Inspector general">inspector general</a>. This position was approved by county voters in 2010. A county judge found that the mandate covered municipal government in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_History">Political History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Political History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1992" title="United States presidential election, 1992">1992</a>, Palm Beach County has supported a Democrat for the presidency. Prior to 1992, the county had been carried by a Republican every four years since <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1948" title="United States presidential election, 1948">1948</a>. Palm Beach County was the center of a nationwide media storm in 2000 when it appeared to have impacted the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Florida,_2000" title="United States presidential election in Florida, 2000">presidential election</a> that year between eventual winner <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>. A major source of controversy was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Butterfly_ballot" title="Butterfly ballot">butterfly ballot</a> used in Palm Beach County, a confusing ballot design which may have caused many voters to mistakenly vote for Reform Party candidate Pat Buchanan instead of Al Gore. Buchanan had an unexpectedly strong showing in the county.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> In the end, Gore carried the county, but Bush captured the state of Florida by 537 votes after the recount was effectively halted by the Supreme Court of the United States in <a href="/wiki/Bush_v._Gore" title="Bush v. Gore">Bush v. Gore</a>.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2004" title="United States presidential election, 2004">2004 presidential election</a>, President Bush garnered more votes in the state, but trailed Democrat <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> by 60.35%-39.05%. During the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_election_in_Florida,_2004" title="United States Senate election in Florida, 2004">United States Senate election</a>, <a href="/wiki/Betty_Castor" title="Betty Castor">Betty Castor</a> (D) carried Palm Beach County against Republican <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mel_Martinez" title="Mel Martinez">Mel Martinez</a> by a slightly wider margin of 22.26%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_election_in_Florida,_2006" title="United States Senate election in Florida, 2006">2006</a>, incumbent Senator <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bill_Nelson_(politician)" title="Bill Nelson (politician)">Bill Nelson</a> (D) trounced <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Harris" title="Katherine Harris">Katherine Harris</a> (R), receiving about 72.54% of the vote. Then-Republican <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Crist" title="Charlie Crist">Charlie Crist</a> was defeated in the county by <a href="/wiki/Jim_Davis_(Florida_politician)" title="Jim Davis (Florida politician)">Jim Davis</a> (D) by 59.71%-38.28%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2008" title="United States presidential election, 2008">2008 presidential election</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> increased the Democratic victory margin from four years earlier and took approximately 61.08% of the vote against <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a> (R) in the county.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Florida_gubernatorial_election,_2010" title="Florida gubernatorial election, 2010">2010 gubernatorial election</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Sink" title="Alex Sink">Alex Sink</a> (D) won Palm Beach County by a margin of 18.67% against <a href="/wiki/Rick_Scott" title="Rick Scott">Rick Scott</a> (R). <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_election_in_Florida,_2010" title="United States Senate election in Florida, 2010">That same year</a>, then-Independent United States Senate candidate and former Governor Crist carried Palm Beach County by just under 3,000 votes, or a margin of only 0.74%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> President Obama, who was <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2012" title="United States presidential election, 2012">re-elected in 2012</a>, won by a smaller margin in the county, with <a href="/wiki/Mitt_Romney" title="Mitt Romney">Mitt Romney</a> managing to receive 41.18% of the vote. During the Class I United States Senate <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_election_in_Florida,_2012" title="United States Senate election in Florida, 2012">seat election in Florida</a>, incumbent Democrat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bill_Nelson_(politician)" title="Bill Nelson (politician)">Bill Nelson</a> garnered 55.2% of the vote against challenger <a href="/wiki/Connie_Mack_IV" title="Connie Mack IV">Connie Mack IV</a> in Palm Beach County.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Former Governor Crist, who became a Democrat, garnered 58.8% of the vote against Governor Scott in the <a href="/wiki/Florida_gubernatorial_election,_2014" title="Florida gubernatorial election, 2014">2014 gubernatorial election</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014elections_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-2014elections-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_Representation">Federal Representation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Federal Representation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a>, Palm Beach County is represented by three Democrats and one Republican: <a href="/wiki/Brian_Mast" title="Brian Mast">Brian Mast</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_18th_congressional_district" title="Florida's 18th congressional district">18th district</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alcee_Hastings" title="Alcee Hastings">Alcee Hastings</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_20th_congressional_district" title="Florida's 20th congressional district">20th district</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ted_Deutch" title="Ted Deutch">Ted Deutch</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_21st_congressional_district" title="Florida's 21st congressional district">21st district</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lois_Frankel" title="Lois Frankel">Lois Frankel</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_22nd_congressional_district" title="Florida's 22nd congressional district">22nd district</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014elections_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-2014elections-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roadways">Roadways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Roadways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An <a href="/wiki/Smart_Growth_America" title="Smart Growth America">advocacy group</a> has criticized Palm Beach County's roadways for being dangerous for non-motorized users.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Local municipalities are working to increase safety, but county and state authorities have been hesitant to modify designs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Expressways">Expressways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Expressways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:I-95.svg"><img alt="I-95.svg" data-file-height="601" data-file-width="601" height="25" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/I-95.svg/25px-I-95.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/I-95.svg/38px-I-95.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/I-95.svg/50px-I-95.svg.png 2x" width="25"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Florida" title="Interstate 95 in Florida">Interstate 95</a></li>
<li><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Florida%27s_Turnpike_shield.png"><img alt="Florida's Turnpike shield.png" data-file-height="277" data-file-width="232" height="30" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Florida%27s_Turnpike_shield.png/25px-Florida%27s_Turnpike_shield.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Florida%27s_Turnpike_shield.png/38px-Florida%27s_Turnpike_shield.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Florida%27s_Turnpike_shield.png/50px-Florida%27s_Turnpike_shield.png 2x" width="25"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Florida%27s_Turnpike" title="Florida's Turnpike">Florida's Turnpike</a></li>
</ul>
<p>I-95 and Florida's Turnpike are controlled-access expressways that serve Palm Beach county. <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_80" title="Florida State Road 80">Southern Boulevard</a> (signed <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_80" title="Florida State Road 80">SR 80</a>/<a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_98_in_Florida" title="U.S. Route 98 in Florida">US 98</a>), which runs east–west through central Palm Beach County, is a partial freeway from Interstate 95 in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach" title="West Palm Beach">West Palm Beach</a> to <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_441_in_Florida" title="U.S. Route 441 in Florida">US 441</a>/<a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_7" title="Florida State Road 7">SR 7</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Palm_Beach" title="Royal Palm Beach">Royal Palm Beach</a>. In the late 1980s, there were plans to construct two additional expressways in Palm Beach County. One was to be an 11.5 miles (18.5 km) toll freeway from Royal Palm Beach to downtown West Palm Beach. It would have run between Belvedere Road and <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_704" title="Florida State Road 704">Okeechobee Boulevard</a>; necessitating the destruction of several homes and churches along its path. The other proposed route was a northern extension of the <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Road_869" title="Florida State Road 869">Sawgrass Expressway</a> which was to be called "University Parkway". The University Parkway would have snaked around suburban developments west of <a href="/wiki/Boca_Raton,_Florida" title="Boca Raton, Florida">Boca Raton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delray_Beach,_Florida" title="Delray Beach, Florida">Delray Beach</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boynton_Beach,_Florida" title="Boynton Beach, Florida">Boynton Beach</a>; its path bordering the <a href="/wiki/Loxahatchee_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Loxahatchee National Wildlife Refuge">Loxahatchee National Wildlife Refuge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Ultimately, both expressways were canceled due to opposition from county residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railroads">Railroads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Palm_Beach_County,_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Railroads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tri-Rail" title="Tri-Rail">Tri-Rail</a> runs along eastern Palm Beach county, adjacent to <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Florida" title="Interstate 95 in Florida">Interstate 95</a> for most of its length. It has stops in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boca_Raton" title="Boca Raton">Boca Raton</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delray_Beach" title="Delray Beach">Delray Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boynton_Beach,_Florida" title="Boynton Beach, Florida">Boynton Beach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Worth,_Florida" title="Lake Worth, Florida">Lake Worth</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach" title="West Palm Beach">West Palm Beach</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mangonia_Park" title="Mangonia Park">Mangonia Park</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>The national inter-city train system, <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a>, offers the <a href="/wiki/Silver_Meteor" title="Silver Meteor">Silver Meteor</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Silver_Star_(Amtrak_train)" title="Silver Star (Amtrak train)">Silver Star</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach" title="West Palm Beach">West Palm Beach station</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delray_Beach" title="Delray Beach">Delray Beach</a>.</p>
